<div id="review_126524598" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/126524598" />
    <a title="Ashley" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/1343864-ashley"><img alt="Ashley" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1597876967p2/1343864.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/126524598?book_show_action=true">Oct 16, 2010</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Ashley" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Ashley" href="/user/show/1343864-ashley">Ashley</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Hardcover 9780451463357" href="/book/show/7116897-blood-rites">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1343864-ashley?shelf=orphalins">orphalins</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1343864-ashley?shelf=audiobooks">audiobooks</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1343864-ashley?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1343864-ashley?shelf=urban-fantasy">urban-fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1343864-ashley?shelf=ridiculously-prolific-authors">ridiculously-prolific-authors</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1343864-ashley?shelf=mysteries">mysteries</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1343864-ashley?shelf=paranormal-and-supernatural">paranormal-and-supernatural</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1343864-ashley?shelf=murder-most-foul">murder-most-foul</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1343864-ashley?shelf=i-vant-to-drink-your-blood">i-vant-to-drink-your-blood</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer126524598" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer11193622597654227362"><b>Re-read, February 2017</b>: So far on this Dresden Files re-read of mine, I've liked all the books better (some significantly so). But this one gave me feeeeelings. I mean, I mostly remembered it for the Harry-goes-undercover-on-the-set-of-a-porno plot, so to say that these feeeeelings were unexpected was a bit of an understatement. <br/><br/>So Harry goes undercover on the set of a porno! His White Court vampire acquaintance, Thomas, has asked him for a favor, to take the director on as a client, to protect </span>
  <span id="freeText11193622597654227362" style="display:none"><b>Re-read, February 2017</b>: So far on this Dresden Files re-read of mine, I've liked all the books better (some significantly so). But this one gave me feeeeelings. I mean, I mostly remembered it for the Harry-goes-undercover-on-the-set-of-a-porno plot, so to say that these feeeeelings were unexpected was a bit of an understatement. <br /><br />So Harry goes undercover on the set of a porno! His White Court vampire acquaintance, Thomas, has asked him for a favor, to take the director on as a client, to protect the cast and crew from an evil eye curse that is taking people out. And this wouldn't be a Dresden Files book if multiple shits didn't hit the fan at the same time. Luckily it's only a couple this time instead of the usual five or so. The Black Court is also in town, and they're gunning for Harry. So for a change of pace, he decides instead of waiting for trouble to come to him, he's just going to kill it all first. With the help of friends (and hired goons), of course.<br /><br />So the part where the feelings come in is that Harry spends a lot of time musing about family in this one, whether because of accidentally attending Murphy's family reunion, or witnessing the dynamics between the Raith clan. So halfway through when he finds out that <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[Thomas is actually his half-brother, and that he's no longer alone <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span>, the whole book ends up crystalizing around their fledgling relationship. Also, Mouse shows up as a puppy, and I forgot how freaking cute he used to be. <br /><br />Not much else to say, other than I really enjoyed revisiting this. Most of my original review still stands, although the things I had problems with (Harry's fight with McCoy, the lingering fight scenes) didn't bother me as much this go-round. As great as the audiobooks are for this series, the one advantage the hard copies have is you can get through the iffy bits muuuch faster.<br /><br /><b>Original Review, February 2012</b>: I continue to be surprised at how much I enjoy this series for as much as I was bored and frustrated by the first three volumes.<br /><br />All through the first three books, I just didn't get the hype. I thought Harry came off as Butcher's attempt to Mary Sue himself into the fictional world, I thought the secondary characters were underdeveloped and underused, and I was mostly bored by all the "exciting" things that Harry constantly had happen to him. And on top of that boredom was a thin layer of disbelief, because seriously, that guy got beaten up so much and acted so stoic and heroic about it all the time that he didn't even read as a real person to me. And then I listened to book four on audio, and I'm still not sure if it's my affection for narrator <a href="https://www.google.com/search?q=james+marsters&amp;hl=en&amp;safe=off&amp;client=firefox-a&amp;hs=sX5&amp;rls=org.mozilla:en-US:official&amp;prmd=imvnsol&amp;tbm=isch&amp;tbo=u&amp;source=univ&amp;sa=X&amp;ei=f1FJT8eBBoqyiQKL0vjaDQ&amp;ved=0CFQQsAQ&amp;biw=1156&amp;bih=818" rel="nofollow noopener">James Marsters</a> that did it or if Butcher's writing actually got better, but the series has grown on me. I still think Harry comes off as a bit of a sacrificial lamb, among other things, but the secondary characters are nicely developed now and Harry's world finally has some emotional texture to it.<br /><br /><i>Blood Rites</i> is the sixth book in <i>The Dresden Files</i> series, which features Harry Dresden as Chicago's only professional wizard. An acquaintance of Harry's -- a White Court vampire (incubi/succubi, basically) named Thomas -- hires him to protect the cast and crew of a porno flick, which seems to be haunted by a mysterious curse. It's Harry's job not only to protect everyone involved, but to find out who's behind it and why, and stop them. He gets way more than he bargained for, as usual. Meanwhile, he also has to deal with a nasty nest full of Black Court vampires that's taken up residence in Chicago, and some personal problems that he really didn't see coming involving revelations about his past. For a majority of the book he also happens to carry a small gray puppy around in one of the many pockets of his trenchcoat, and it pops up in the narrative every once in a while to inject some much needed cute. <br /><br />There's a lot less sex in this book than you would expect from a story involving porn stars, porn filmmakers and incubi and succubi running around all over the place, but I enjoyed the wackiness of the setting, and Butcher treated the porn stars like actual characters rather than giving in to the tempting impulse to portray them as nothing more than their jobs (although I do think he was a bit naive about the whole porn thing, if I'm being honest about it). I really liked what this book did with Harry's relationships with several key characters, namely Thomas <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[(who turns out to be his half-brother) <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span>, Murphy (who is actually given things to do nowadays and characterization beyond her role as backup to Harry's insanity, and Harry's mentor, Ebenezar McCoy (even if I do happen to think that Harry was being a bit of a drama queen about the secrets Ebenezar spills late in the book).<br /><br />I'm still a little frustrated by Butcher's style, but it's most a personal frustration based on my own likes and dislikes. I'm still frustrated by little things, like the way he uses "glowered" every five seconds, and the way he has characters become quiet a lot as a way to code anger and badassery. I also think his fight scenes go on WAY too long. The whole Black Court vampire plot was kind of boring, even though Butcher has Murphy disarming a bomb with no pants on. I wanted more White Court shiznat and porn-set antics. Also, way more Thomas. And it continues to become more and more apparent that while Harry isn't necessarily sexist, he certainly thinks of women in annoyingly chivalric, protective terms*, like a modern day caveman. But to his credit, it's in sort of an endearing way. The scene where he feels betrayed by his mentor made me angry. I think we were supposed to side with Harry instead of Ebenezer, but instead I just found myself becoming angry with Harry for being stupid. I did like the ending, and I thought Lord Raith was a genuinely scary bad guy, and that he was dealt with by both Butcher and Harry in a clever way.<br /><br />*<i>I'm convinced that Jim Butcher is permanently stuck in the 90s just by the way he has Murphy dress and the things he makes Harry think are cool. Also, by looking at his bio picture. That dude seriously needs a haircut.</i><br /><br />I'll probably pick up the next book on audiobook whenever it becomes available at my library, but I'm more excited about this series than I have been since I started reading it a couple of years ago. I'm glad Butcher is finally allowing his characters to interact with one another, and I'm glad he's finally allowing Harry to have some real relationships. It makes for much better and more interesting reading.</span>
  <a data-text-id="11193622597654227362" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="☕️Kimberly  " class="user" itemprop="url" name="☕️Kimberly  " href="/user/show/5082615-kimberly">☕️Kimberly  </a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Audiobook 9781101222294" href="/book/show/8181595-blood-rites">review of another edition</a>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2527216060" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer12021793176724941464"><strong>Reason to grab your headphones 🎧 and listen to Blood Rites</strong><br/><br/><em>*Like most urban fantasy series the books share an overall arc and the relationships and characters experience growth that are best read in the order of their release. Each book however contains a complete case that Harry takes on and tries to survive. *winks*</em><br/> <br/> 	 I love when I am into a series and suddenly characters and connections click into place. In <em>Blood Rite</em> we learn much about Thomas and Harry. <br/> 	 Harry is becoming a little jaded b</span>
  <span id="freeText12021793176724941464" style="display:none"><strong>Reason to grab your headphones 🎧 and listen to Blood Rites</strong><br /><br /><em>*Like most urban fantasy series the books share an overall arc and the relationships and characters experience growth that are best read in the order of their release. Each book however contains a complete case that Harry takes on and tries to survive. *winks*</em><br /> <br /> 	 I love when I am into a series and suddenly characters and connections click into place. In <em>Blood Rite</em> we learn much about Thomas and Harry. <br /> 	 Harry is becoming a little jaded but we meet Mouse and it reminded me that Harry has a softer, gentler side. <br /> 	 Thomas asks Harry to take on a case, and despite saying no and protesting loudly he takes the job. Harry lives hand to mouth and is once again broke sealing his fate. <br /> 	 The case seems simple enough. Protect the producer of  an adult film. Harry goes undercover at the studio. I laughed at the humorous situations Harry finds himself in even as he has to dodge danger. <br /> 	 Harry soon finds himself protecting Thomas. His own sister is vying for him. Butcher pulled me into the story as he connected characters and focused on family. <br /> 	 I love when an author throws surprises at me. And surprise me he did! <br /> 	 Vampire, incubus, reveals, old and new characters helped round out the tale giving way to suspense, surprises and lots of non-stop action. <br /> <br /><a href="https://caffeinatedbookreviewer.com/2019/01/blood-rites-by-jim-butcher.html" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener"> This review was originally posted at Caffeinated Reviewer</a></span>

<div id="review_127027104" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/127027104" />
    <a title="Kelly H. (Maybedog)" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/1059653-kelly-h-maybedog"><img alt="Kelly H. (Maybedog)" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1366465767p2/1059653.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/127027104?book_show_action=true">Oct 19, 2010</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Kelly H. (Maybedog)" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Kelly H. (Maybedog)" href="/user/show/1059653-kelly-h-maybedog">Kelly H. (Maybedog)</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1059653-kelly-h-maybedog?shelf=what-male-protagonist">what-male-protagonist</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1059653-kelly-h-maybedog?shelf=what-modern-fantasy">what-modern-fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1059653-kelly-h-maybedog?shelf=what-vampires">what-vampires</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1059653-kelly-h-maybedog?shelf=why-favorite-author">why-favorite-author</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1059653-kelly-h-maybedog?shelf=why-favorite-series">why-favorite-series</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1059653-kelly-h-maybedog?shelf=what-fae">what-fae</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1059653-kelly-h-maybedog?shelf=what-not-mm">what-not-mm</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer127027104" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer7629637809588688677">Despite the fact that this book needed an editor to point out places where the character gets up from a chair twice in the same paragraph without ever sitting down again or when he eats 3 breakfasts at three different places while seeing a doctor at the last minute between the last two (er, what time is breakfast at the last place?) without ever even mentioning he was full... Okay I'm going to pause there and add a period because even though that isn't a complete sentence, it's too dang long.<br/><br/>Any</span>
  <span id="freeText7629637809588688677" style="display:none">Despite the fact that this book needed an editor to point out places where the character gets up from a chair twice in the same paragraph without ever sitting down again or when he eats 3 breakfasts at three different places while seeing a doctor at the last minute between the last two (er, what time is breakfast at the last place?) without ever even mentioning he was full... Okay I'm going to pause there and add a period because even though that isn't a complete sentence, it's too dang long.<br /><br />Anyway, despite that, Blood Rites is another great tale from Butcher. It's fast paced adventure, starting with page one and leaving with not a cliffhanger exactly but a desire to read the next book RIGHT NOW. He's great at doing that with his chapters, too. I'd promise myself I'd stop reading at the end of the chapter but almost always it ends with something that made me want to keep reading. <br /><br />The characters are likable, with strong interesting women (no more wilting flower girlfriend), and believable actions and emotions. I love his concept and development of the emotion vampire. Although at times certain plot devices seemed rather convenient, the book had two equally strong narratives through out that co-mingled nicely, twists and turns and loads of surprises and revelations about series characters. <br /><br />At times funny, at times tragic, in all, Blood Rites is a good, solid read for those looking for a fun urban fantasy. Oh, and a puppy! Dresden + puppy = Kelly happy place. </span>
  <a data-text-id="7629637809588688677" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

<div id="review_176153168" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/176153168" />
    <a title="carol. " class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/3978225-carol"><img alt="carol. " src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1307934801p2/3978225.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">

<div id="review_1270519611" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1270519611" />
    <a title="Luffy" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/7407364-luffy"><img alt="Luffy" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1606210775p2/7407364.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1270519611?book_show_action=true">May 03, 2015</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Luffy" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Luffy" href="/user/show/7407364-luffy">Luffy</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/7407364-luffy?shelf=5-star">5-star</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1270519611" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer2235102781663465329">So far I've found the Dresden books very unbalanced. The huge space reserved for a usually sprawling finale often messed with the clever, heartfelt, carefully dosed, and, sometimes, funny and smart precedents. What has changed is yours truly. I have learned why Dresden, the book series, has garnered so many fans. Its irreverent take on the little problems of life, which laces and binds the opening chapters, has been something I didn't detect with the previous 5 books. But here, I know and acknow</span>
  <span id="freeText2235102781663465329" style="display:none">So far I've found the Dresden books very unbalanced. The huge space reserved for a usually sprawling finale often messed with the clever, heartfelt, carefully dosed, and, sometimes, funny and smart precedents. What has changed is yours truly. I have learned why Dresden, the book series, has garnered so many fans. Its irreverent take on the little problems of life, which laces and binds the opening chapters, has been something I didn't detect with the previous 5 books. But here, I know and acknowledge its value. Jim Butcher will never kill his main characters, will never stop writing overlong climaxes, will keep on making brilliant jokes, but as long as he is not jaded and not too drunk on his success, I'll be a distant follower, though not a genuine fan. Not yet.<br /><br /> Along with a new insight into the workings of the book, I think many of the problems, namely those of pacing and gravitas, were absent in book six. This is a book that a few people have expressed disappointment with, but personally I warmed up to the film noir vibe and the dated crime drama deja vu feeling it exuded. The author combined many ideas from Hong Kong movies to Agatha Christie to comic books to Buffy to craft Blood Rites. I found the treatment of the story's casualties decent enough. There were revelations galore which dog the vacuum that is the past of the hero, Harry Dresden. I prefer revelations to action fueled twists. Twists sometimes feel forced. Their lack certainly improved the feel of the plot, which moved incessantly forward, and there was not any filler. What I wanted to say was that Jim Butcher was inspired for this book.<br /><br /> But would someone tell me who was the first author to come up with the concept of Hunger, with a big letter H, in the vampire subgenre? It's irritating as hell and while at first the effect was theatrical and pretentious, now it's ridiculous, pejorative, and annoying. Hunger is just the appetite of the bloodthirsty. End of. Now I'm going to mention my favorite character of the series; step forward Karrin Murphy. She is both charismatic and elusive. By that I mean that here, I was okay with her playing a small role, and keep away from the climax. That has happened before and it was proof that Murphy was a versatile character. In this book, I would have been fine with seeing her last at her family reunion, exceptionally wearing a dress to please her mom, being herself. Yet I had no problem with her taking part in the action. I do, however, get tired of her shedding blood, and small things like the use of her limbs, in the line of what is not even duty. There has been enough debate about inflicting pain on fictional women in various media and I don't have any new thing to mention but I hope the next books in the series make Murphy take a back seat towards the climactic hijinks. By the way, I loved the Kinkaid character almost as much. All of these elements make me think that Jim Butcher is not making stuff as he goes along. He has a plan. He knows how everything hangs together. He knows how it will end. I want to know too. So yeah, I do.</span>
  <a data-text-id="2235102781663465329" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_1101494819" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1101494819" />
    <a title="Richard" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/8386404-richard"><img alt="Richard" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1351707681p2/8386404.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1101494819?book_show_action=true">Nov 09, 2014</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Richard" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Richard" href="/user/show/8386404-richard">Richard</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9781841494036" href="/book/show/234553.Blood_Rites">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/8386404-richard?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1101494819" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer1541144142637267954">9/10<br/> <br/>This was probably the best outing in the Dresden world for me to date. The series could have gone one of two ways really; tedious and repetitive with stale characters with a too jokey style or an ever increasing amount of world building with entertaining characters with a whimsical style that amused. Luckily, the later seems to be more apt for me and I love that with each novel there is more information provided, like a slow drip feeding, about the world and characters to draw you in furthe</span>
  <span id="freeText1541144142637267954" style="display:none">9/10<br /> <br />This was probably the best outing in the Dresden world for me to date. The series could have gone one of two ways really; tedious and repetitive with stale characters with a too jokey style or an ever increasing amount of world building with entertaining characters with a whimsical style that amused. Luckily, the later seems to be more apt for me and I love that with each novel there is more information provided, like a slow drip feeding, about the world and characters to draw you in further.<br /> <br />There is a term for how this book starts, I can’t recall it now, but it starts in the thick of Harry in some action with one of his ever growing list of (sort of) sidekicks. This has been used a couple of times in the series and I have to applaud it as it gets you deep into the book without realising. By the time you come up for breath you realise you’ve read a massive chunk of the book and the story is well on the way.<br /> <br />Harry is drawn into an investigation onto an adult film set to try and work out why certain women are being targeted and killed on the set. There are plenty of humorous jokes throughout this part and it is quite the light read. The second half of the book is more complex and draws on the previous novels for back-story and gives Harry a different kind of enemy to battle and adds further layers to the world and characters in it. Both contrasting styles helped shape the overall book and it worked well.<br /> <br />As I mentioned, this was my favourite book in the series to date. I look forward to reading the rest and think this series will be one of those that when all is said and done I will re-read from the start. I’ve noticed in a couple of reviews there were people who got annoyed at certain things about the series but these have completely passed me by. Now if you excuse me, the band wagon is driving by and I must jump on it.<br /> <br />If you enjoy this try: “Going Postal” by Terry Pratchett</span>
  <a data-text-id="1541144142637267954" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_128058808" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/128058808" />
    <a title="Jim" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/695116-jim"><img alt="Jim" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1340192527p2/695116.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/128058808?book_show_action=true">Oct 26, 2010</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Jim" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Jim" href="/user/show/695116-jim">Jim</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/695116-jim?shelf=3series">3series</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/695116-jim?shelf=1paper">1paper</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/695116-jim?shelf=paranormal-urban">paranormal-urban</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/695116-jim?shelf=2fiction">2fiction</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer128058808" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer8713146161442105509">It was a pretty good romp in many ways, but I was highly ticked off my numerous logical flaws, especially around the middle of the book. Harry's staff is very important, but through sheer sloppiness, Butcher manages to have it in two places. <br/><br/>He also puts a manual car - one that has been a stick throughout the series & we just read was hard for Harry to drive due to a wounded leg - into 'drive' instead of first. A sentence or two later, he shifts into second. <br/><br/>Power is out in the city - a big deal</span>
  <span id="freeText8713146161442105509" style="display:none">It was a pretty good romp in many ways, but I was highly ticked off my numerous logical flaws, especially around the middle of the book. Harry's staff is very important, but through sheer sloppiness, Butcher manages to have it in two places. <br /><br />He also puts a manual car - one that has been a stick throughout the series &amp; we just read was hard for Harry to drive due to a wounded leg - into 'drive' instead of first. A sentence or two later, he shifts into second. <br /><br />Power is out in the city - a big deal is made out of this &amp; the plot is hinging on it - but Harry &amp; Billy take the elevator. A few paragraphs later, a big deal is made out of Harry having to walk up steps due to no power. Please!!! <br /><br />These are major logical flaws that just slam an otherwise decent book &amp; they're nothing but sloppy. There's no excuse for them. A bit of free proofreading or a decent editor would easily have caught them.<br /><br />As interesting as the series is in other ways, I just can't stand the sloppiness &amp; have to take a break.</span>
  <a data-text-id="8713146161442105509" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

  function submitShelfLink(unique_id, book_id, shelf_id, shelf_name, submit_form, exclusive) {
    var checkbox_id = 'shelf_name_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    var element = document.getElementById(checkbox_id)

    var checked = element.checked
    if (checked && exclusive) {
      // can't uncheck a radio by clicking it!
      return
    }
    if(document.getElementById("savingMessage")){
      Element.show('savingMessage')
    }
    var element_id = 'shelfInDropdownName_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    Element.update(element_id, "saving...");
    if (submit_form) {
      Element.hide('shelfDropdown_' + unique_id)
      var form = document.getElementById('addBookForm' + book_id)
      if (form) {
        form.shelf.value = shelf_name
        form.onsubmit()
      }
    }
    else {
      var action = checked ? 'remove' : ''
      element.checked = !element.checked
      new Ajax.Request('/shelf/add_to_shelf', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name)}, parameters:'book_id=' + book_id + '&name=' + shelf_name + '&a=' + action + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('FO0qc57+CwGijeyFIMqYTwx6zvxpVRn2cSxdEufD/1c6Kcb+OQMAZGD/eW4NF8OvpJFaGcoI6qF2e+mfK4qBUg==')})
    }
  }

  function shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name) {
    Element.update('shelfListfalse_' + book_id, request.responseText)
    afterShelfSave(checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name.escapeHTML())
  }

  function refreshGroupBox(group_id, book_id) {
    new Ajax.Updater('addGroupBooks' + book_id + '', '/group/add_book_box', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){refreshGroupBoxComplete(request, book_id);}, parameters:'id=' + group_id + '&book_id=' + book_id + '&refresh=true' + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('qrli9cRIADRCUHWDF5HUsW5/wX9HgqIdcDYVyteSouiEfY54Y7ULUYAi4Gg6TI9RxpRVmuTfUUp3YaFHG9vc7Q==')})
  }

<span id="freeTextContainer18141503447348970439">Jim Butcher is the author of the Dresden Files, the Codex Alera, and a new steampunk series, the Cinder Spires. His resume includes a laundry list of skills which were useful a couple of centuries ago, and he plays guitar quite badly. An avid gamer, he plays tabletop games in varying systems, a variety of video games on PC and console, and LARPs whenever he can make time for it. Jim currently resi</span>
  <span id="freeText18141503447348970439" style="display:none">Jim Butcher is the author of the Dresden Files, the Codex Alera, and a new steampunk series, the Cinder Spires. His resume includes a laundry list of skills which were useful a couple of centuries ago, and he plays guitar quite badly. An avid gamer, he plays tabletop games in varying systems, a variety of video games on PC and console, and LARPs whenever he can make time for it. Jim currently resides mostly inside his own head, but his head can generally be found in his home town of Independence, Missouri.<br /><br />Jim goes by the moniker Longshot in a number of online locales. He came by this name in the early 1990′s when he decided he would become a published author. Usually only 3 in 1000 who make such an attempt actually manage to become published; of those, only 1 in 10 make enough money to call it a living. The sale of a second series was the breakthrough that let him beat the long odds against attaining a career as a novelist.<br /><br />All the same, he refuses to change his nickname.<br /></span>
